@kikisuzumiya or when a vtuber does it
To sum all of THAT up, I took the more grounded approach and took being a #vtuber as vaguely as being a #youtuber. It's a way to present yourself and what you want to share with the world, and the rest is up to you.  I can only hope that it worked.
But, this #vtuber thing is something I like, even though my interpretation is different. I haven't even really spoken to other vtubers... but I can certainly say that it's the main reason why I've made more videos than ever before.
Going over ALL of that would be quite dry, I think. But since I'm not just having fun and trying to do something educational, I knew I wouldn't exactly be popular with what I think the #vtuber community likes. I'm not doing anything similar, or even really paying attention...
Because of that, I instead became a #vtuber to support the videos I've been wanting to make, instead of aimlessly playing around with a digital persona. 'Eiri' existed long before this. #Megaman11 was the perfect moment to start, since I wanted to fully document my time with it.
What is probably the most contentious part, is that I don't fully consider myself a #vtuber. It's a trending word this year, but many of the pieces for a real-time digital avatar started to appear many years ago. I think many people got the idea independently, before 2017~'18.
So I kinda wrote a behind-the-scenes, post-mortem of my time so far as a #vtuber, (which is what the montage video was for,) but given the length, making a video retrospective seems a bit much. It also didn't seem appropriate for the channel, so I'll post the major notes here.
